      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2363295113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer687969573744872545"><i>Adjustment Day</i> is like the idiot child of <i>Fight Club</i>. It is a bigger, stupider, shallower imitation for the Internet age.<br/><br/>That might seem unfairly harsh, but is impossible to avoid comparing <i>Adjustment Day</i> to <i>Fight Club</i>. Palahniuk does it himself in book, when he outright asserts the purposes of each book (on page 157 of my copy). As far as I am concerned, that begs for comparisons. In this comparison, <i>Adjustment Day</i> falls short. <br/><br/><i>Adjustment Day</i> is full of social commentary. That's fine; social co</span>
  <span id="freeText687969573744872545" style="display:none"><i>Adjustment Day</i> is like the idiot child of <i>Fight Club</i>. It is a bigger, stupider, shallower imitation for the Internet age.<br /><br />That might seem unfairly harsh, but is impossible to avoid comparing <i>Adjustment Day</i> to <i>Fight Club</i>. Palahniuk does it himself in book, when he outright asserts the purposes of each book (on page 157 of my copy). As far as I am concerned, that begs for comparisons. In this comparison, <i>Adjustment Day</i> falls short. <br /><br /><i>Adjustment Day</i> is full of social commentary. That's fine; social commentary was one of the strengths of <i>Fight Club</i>. However, the social commentary in this novel is <b>bad</b>. First, it is unforgivably preachy. It talks down to the reader with whatever random political pronouncements and cultural comments Palahniuk had lying around. Imagine the worst college dropout pontificating on YouTube about how he knows "what's really going on", and you'll have a good idea of the insufferable tone of <i>Adjustment Day</i>.<br /><br />Second, even worse is that <i>Adjustment Day</i> preaches absolute bullshit. Sure, it has some of the message of self-actualization that formed the core of <i>Fight Club</i>. Unfortunately, that message is buried under some of the worst dreck I have ever read. Palahniuk repeats the biggest lies of the modern era, including Holocaust denial, the moon landing conspiracy, and the idea that education prevents critical thought. More fundamentally, the books seems to be anti-intellectual, anti-science, misogynistic, pro-segregation, and pro-violence. Rather than transgressing as did <i>Fight Club</i>, <i>Adjustment Day</i> panders to the lowest common denominator of our current dysfunctional society.<br /><br />The writing itself does the book no favors. It is raw, as you would expect from a successor to <i>Fight Club</i>. It never grabbed me though. It felt more obligatory than challenging. Also, this book is a mix of unlabeled sections of different subplots. The subplots jump around in time and space. I was further annoyed by the number of pop culture and literary references, including several to Palahniuk and his own works. These references will ensure that the book becomes dated in a way <i>Fight Club</i> never has. These authorial decisions added to the feeling that this book is merely fan fiction written on some disreputable web forum.<br /><br />The story was similarly disappointing. The buildup to the eponymous Adjustment Day is a pale imitation of Project Mayhem. The aftermath includes two slow motion dystopian disasters in Caucasia and Gaysia, and a utopia in Blacktopia. The story borrows heavily from other works like <i>1984</i> and <i>The Handmaid's Tale</i> and conspiracy theories for a thoroughly unremarkable plot. It really is just a vehicle for the commentary, which as I said is crap.<br /><br />Internet-based fan fiction for <i>Fight Club</i>. I can't think of a better way to describe <i>Adjustment Day</i>. I found the book painful in all the wrong ways. I may try another Palahniuk book, but only because he is my best friend's favorite author. I will never touch this book again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="687969573744872545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2379618141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2379618141" />
    <a title="Rachel Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57219804-rachel-christine"><img alt="Rachel Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541459152p2/57219804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2379618141?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Christine" href="/user/show/57219804-rachel-christine">Rachel Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2379618141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5760323121405373169">⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ <br/>I am a big fan of Palahniuk's earlier works (Invisible Monsters, Fight Club, Lullaby) and had the opportunity to meet him at a book signing for this release. I had high expectations going into this book, and while I did like it, there were several parts of it that just didn't work for me.<br/><br/>This book is clearly a satire on our current socioeconomic and political state. It expands on our dissastifcation and fears with the world, and paints a picture of "what would really happen if we rid ou</span>
  <span id="freeText5760323121405373169" style="display:none">⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ <br />I am a big fan of Palahniuk's earlier works (Invisible Monsters, Fight Club, Lullaby) and had the opportunity to meet him at a book signing for this release. I had high expectations going into this book, and while I did like it, there were several parts of it that just didn't work for me.<br /><br />This book is clearly a satire on our current socioeconomic and political state. It expands on our dissastifcation and fears with the world, and paints a picture of "what would really happen if we rid ourselves of the corrupt 'swamp' of policiticians, investment bankers, and real estate moguls and started over?" <br />I enjoy dystopian books and found many parts of it hilairous. However, the structure of the book leaves a lot to be desired. <br /><br />There are so many characters and storylines to keep track of, that I often found myself having to go back through the pages to figure out who that character was and what had been happening to them before. Usually I like books with multiple storylines, but Adjustment Day had way too many (I think 6 or 7?). I feel like a majority of the characters were underdevloped, simply because there were too many for proper development to happen within 300 pages. I would have really liked less storylines and more depth in a select few. The book reads like an anarchist manifesto a la Project Mayhem in many spots and I found some of the "Talbottisms" stated throughout to be very repetitive. There were also way too many pop cultural references smattered across the book. Some I knew, but there were just too many for me to look up while I was reading, and I feel I may have missed something by ot understanding them. <br /><br />As a whole, this book wasn't really for me, but I still love Chuck Palahniuk and hope his next book is more enjoyable!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5760323121405373169" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('27m0FKpTgGQcRxH1RpjRaBD1CVS1PApwwIVTaCfxEf/hn93GEQ1JDLtspZSxbdu3xqrunHuxhBeb+xXZ6rLjZQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qsje7oTvjlSAZCGWe8dytnnQZLbckwVj2NyrBJkunkGQ7rc8P7FHPCdPlfeMMnhpr4+DfhIeiwSDou21VG1s2w==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2546.Chuck_Palahniuk">About Chuck Palahniuk</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2546.Chuck_Palahniuk"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1391203076p3/2546.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/2546.Chuck_Palahniuk">Chuck Palahniuk
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
124,902
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15968876267060548185">Written in stolen moments under truck chassis and on park benches to a soundtrack of The Downward Spiral and Pablo Honey, <i>Fight Club</i> came into existence. The adaptation of <i>Fight Club</i> was a flop at the box office, but achieved cult status on DVD. The film’s popularity drove sales of the novel. Chuck put out two novels in 1999, <i>Survivor</i> and <i>Invisible Monsters</i>. <i>Choke</i>, published in 2001, became Chuck’</span>
  <span id="freeText15968876267060548185" style="display:none">Written in stolen moments under truck chassis and on park benches to a soundtrack of The Downward Spiral and Pablo Honey, <i>Fight Club</i> came into existence. The adaptation of <i>Fight Club</i> was a flop at the box office, but achieved cult status on DVD. The film’s popularity drove sales of the novel. Chuck put out two novels in 1999, <i>Survivor</i> and <i>Invisible Monsters</i>. <i>Choke</i>, published in 2001, became Chuck’s first New York Times bestseller. Chuck’s work has always been infused with personal experience, and his next novel, <i>Lullaby</i>, was no exception. Chuck credits writing <i>Lullaby</i> with helping him cope with the tragic death of his father. <i>Diary</i> and the non-fiction guide to Portland, <i>Fugitives and Refugees</i>, were released in 2003. While on the road in support of <i>Diary</i>, Chuck began reading a short story entitled 'Guts,' which would eventually become part of the novel <i>Haunted</i>.<br /><br />In the years that followed, he continued to write, publishing the bestselling <i>Rant, Snuff, Pygmy, Tell-All, a 'remix' of Invisible Monsters, Damned</i>, and most recently, <i>Doomed</i>. <br /><br />Chuck also enjoys giving back to his fans, and teaching the art of storytelling has been an important part of that. In 2004, Chuck began submitting essays to ChuckPalahniuk.net on the craft of writing. These were 'How To' pieces, straight out of Chuck's personal bag of tricks, based on the tenants of minimalism he learned from Tom Spanbauer. Every month, a “Homework Assignment” would accompany the lesson, so Workshop members could apply what they had learned. (all 36 of these essays can currently be found on The Cult's sister-site, LitReactor.com).<br /><br />Then, in 2009, Chuck increased his involvement by committing to read and review a selection of fan-written stories each month. The best stories are currently set to be published in <i>Burnt Tongues</i>, a forthcoming anthology, with an introduction written by Chuck himself. <br /><br />His next novel, <i>Beautiful You</i>, is due out in October 2014.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15968876267060548185" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
